<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">
<li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_aaa"><b><a href="#ref_aaa">^</a></b></span> The <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Denmark" title="Monarchy of Denmark">monarchy of Denmark</a> reached the Faroes in 1380 with the reign of <a href="/wiki/Olaf_II_of_Denmark" title="Olaf II of Denmark">Olaf II of Denmark</a>.</li>
<li value="2"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bbb"><b><a href="#ref_bbb">^</a></b></span> The Faroes, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> were Norwegian possessions until 1814, as Norway was united with Denmark.</li>
<li value="3"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ccc"><b><a href="#ref_ccc">^</a></b></span> The currency, printed with Faroese motifs, is issued <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/At_par" title="At par">at par</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Danish_krone" title="Danish krone">Danish krone</a>, uses the same sizes and standards as Danish coins and <a href="/wiki/Banknote" title="Banknote">banknotes</a> and incorporates the same security features. Faroese <i>krónur</i> (singular <i>króna</i>) share the Danish <a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> code "DKK".</li>
</ol>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Faroe Islands</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ɛər/: 'are' in 'bare'">ɛər</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>: <span lang="fo" xml:lang="fo"><i>Føroyar</i></span> <small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ˈfœɹjaɹ]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <span lang="da" xml:lang="da"><i>Færøerne</i></span>, <small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Danish" title="Help:IPA/Danish">[ˈfæɐ̯øːˀɐnə]</a></span>), sometimes called the <b>Faeroe Islands</b>, are an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Sea" title="Norwegian Sea">Norwegian Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic</a>, about halfway between <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, 320 kilometres (200 miles) north-northwest of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. The islands are an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">autonomous country</a> within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" title="Kingdom of Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Embargo2014_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Embargo2014-8">[8]</a></sup> Their area is about 1,400 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> (541 square miles) with a population of 50,030 in April 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Faroe_Islands_in_figures_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Faroe_Islands_in_figures-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Faroes' terrain is rugged, and the islands have a <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate#Subpolar_variety_.28Cfc.29" title="Oceanic climate">subpolar oceanic climate (Cfc)</a>: windy, wet, cloudy and cool. Despite this island group's northerly latitude, temperatures average above freezing throughout the year because of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.</p>
<p>Between 1035 and 1814, the Faroes were part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway_(872%E2%80%931397)" title="Kingdom of Norway (872–1397)">Hereditary Kingdom of Norway</a>. In 1814, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kiel" title="Treaty of Kiel">Treaty of Kiel</a> granted Denmark control over the islands, along with two other Norwegian island possessions: <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>. The Faroe Islands have been a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-governing" title="Self-governing">self-governing</a> country within the Kingdom of Denmark since 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The Faroese have control of most domestic matters. Areas that remain the responsibility of Denmark include <a href="/wiki/Danish_Defence" title="Danish Defence">military defence</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Police_of_Denmark" title="Police of Denmark">police department</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Justice_Minister_of_Denmark" title="Justice Minister of Denmark">justice department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Denmark)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (Denmark)">foreign affairs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> However, as they are not part of the same customs area as Denmark, the Faroe Islands have an independent trade policy and can establish trade agreements with other states. The islands also have representation in the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council" title="Nordic Council">Nordic Council</a> as members of the Danish delegation. The people of the Faroe Islands also compete as a national team in certain sports.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, the name <i><span lang="da" xml:lang="da">Færøerne</span></i> may reflect an Old Norse word <i><span lang="non" xml:lang="non">fær</span></i> (sheep). The morpheme <i><span lang="da" xml:lang="da">øerne</span></i> represents a plural (with definite article) of <i><span lang="da" xml:lang="da">ø</span></i> (island) in Danish. The Danish name thus translates as "the islands of sheep". In <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, the name appears as <i><span lang="fo" xml:lang="fo">Føroyar</span></i>. <i><span lang="fo" xml:lang="fo">Oyar</span></i> represents the plural of <i><span lang="fo" xml:lang="fo">oy</span></i>, older Faroese for "island". The modern Faroese word for island is <i>oyggj</i>. In the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a>, their name is sometimes spelled "Faeroe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(September 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="History of the Faroe Islands">History of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<p>Archaeological evidence shows settlers living on the Faroe Islands in two successive periods prior to the arrival of the Norse, the first between 300 and 600 CE and the second between 600 and 800 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Scientists from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Aberdeen" title="University of Aberdeen">University of Aberdeen</a> have also found early cereal pollen from domesticated plants, which further suggests people may have lived on the islands before the Vikings arrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Archaeologist Mike Church noted that <a href="/wiki/Dicuil" title="Dicuil">Dicuil</a> (see below) mentioned what may have been the Faroes. He also suggested that the people living there might have been from Ireland, Scotland or Scandinavia, possibly with groups from all three areas settling there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>A Latin account of a voyage made by <a href="/wiki/Brendan" title="Brendan">Brendan</a>, an Irish monastic saint who lived around 484–578, includes a description of <i>insulae</i> (islands) resembling the Faroe Islands. This association, however, is far from conclusive in its description.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dicuil" title="Dicuil">Dicuil</a>, an Irish monk of the early <a href="/wiki/9th_century" title="9th century">9th century</a>, wrote a more definite account. In his geographical work <i>De mensura orbis terrae</i> he claimed he had reliable information of <i>heremitae ex nostra Scotia</i> ("hermits from our land of Ireland/Scotland") who had lived on the northerly islands of Britain for almost a hundred years until the arrival of Norse pirates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Norsemen settled the islands c. 800, bringing <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse#Old_West_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old West Norse</a>, which evolved into the modern <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese language</a>. According to Icelandic sagas such as <i>Færeyjar Saga</i>, one of the best known men in the island was <a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%B3ndur_%C3%AD_G%C3%B8tu" title="Tróndur í Gøtu">Tróndur í Gøtu</a>, a descendant of Scandinavian chiefs who had settled in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, Ireland. Tróndur led the battle against Sigmund Brestursson, the Norwegian monarchy and the Norwegian church.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_Islands,_1767,_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="693" data-file-width="1254" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Faroe_Islands%2C_1767%2C_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG/220px-Faroe_Islands%2C_1767%2C_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Faroe_Islands%2C_1767%2C_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG/330px-Faroe_Islands%2C_1767%2C_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Faroe_Islands%2C_1767%2C_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG/440px-Faroe_Islands%2C_1767%2C_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_Islands,_1767,_as_seen_by_Yves_de_Kerguelen_Tr%C3%A9marec.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Faroe Islands as seen by the French navigator <a href="/wiki/Yves-Joseph_de_Kerguelen-Tr%C3%A9marec" title="Yves-Joseph de Kerguelen-Trémarec">Yves-Joseph de Kerguelen-Trémarec</a> in 1767</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Norse and <a href="/wiki/Norse%E2%80%93Gaels" title="Norse–Gaels">Norse–Gael</a> settlers probably did not come directly from Scandinavia, but rather from Norse communities surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Isles" title="Northern Isles">Northern Isles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a> of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> islands. A traditional name for the islands in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, <i>Na Scigirí</i>, possibly refers to the <i>(Eyja-)Skeggjar</i> "(Island-)Beards", a nickname given to island dwellers.</p>
<p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A6reyinga_saga" title="Færeyinga saga">Færeyinga saga</a></i>, more emigrants left Norway who did not approve of the monarchy of <a href="/wiki/Harald_Fairhair" title="Harald Fairhair">Harald Fairhair</a> (ruled c. 872 to 930). These people settled the Faroes around the end of the 9th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Early in the 11th century, <a href="/wiki/Sigmundur_Brestisson" title="Sigmundur Brestisson">Sigmundur Brestisson</a> (961–1005) – whose clan had flourished in the southern islands before invaders from the northern islands almost <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">exterminated</a> it – escaped to Norway. He was sent back to take possession of the islands for <a href="/wiki/Olaf_Tryggvason" title="Olaf Tryggvason">Olaf Tryggvason</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Norway" title="Monarchy of Norway">King of Norway</a> from 995 to 1000. Sigmundur introduced Christianity, forcing Tróndur í Gøtu to convert or face beheading and, though Sigmundur was subsequently murdered, Norwegian taxation was upheld. Norwegian control of the Faroes continued until 1814, although, when the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway_(872%E2%80%931397)" title="Kingdom of Norway (872–1397)">Kingdom of Norway (872–1397)</a> entered the <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_Union" title="Kalmar Union">Kalmar Union</a> with Denmark, it gradually resulted in Danish control of the islands. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> reached the Faroes in 1538. When the union between Denmark and Norway dissolved as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kiel" title="Treaty of Kiel">Treaty of Kiel</a> in 1814, Denmark retained possession of the Faroe Islands; Norway itself was joined in a union with Sweden.</p>
<p>The trade monopoly in the Faroe Islands was abolished in 1856, after which the area developed as a modern fishing nation with its own <a href="/wiki/Fishing_fleet" title="Fishing fleet">fishing fleet</a>. The national awakening from 1888 initially arose from a struggle to maintain the <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese language</a> and was thus <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culturally</a> oriented, but after 1906 it became more <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">political</a> with the foundation of <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Faroe_Islands" title="List of political parties in the Faroe Islands">political parties of the Faroe Islands</a>.</p>
<p>On 12 April 1940 <a href="/wiki/British_occupation_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="British occupation of the Faroe Islands">British troops occupied the Faroe Islands</a>, shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Weser%C3%BCbung" title="Operation Weserübung">German invasion of Denmark</a> on 9 April 1940. In 1942–1943 the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Monmouthshire_Royal_Engineers" title="Royal Monmouthshire Royal Engineers">Royal Engineers</a>, under the leadership of Lt. Col. William Law MC, built the only airport in the Faroe Islands, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1gar_Airport" title="Vágar Airport">Vágar Airport</a>. Control of the islands reverted to Denmark following the war, but in 1948 <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> was introduced, with a high degree of local autonomy. In 1973 the Faroe Islands declined to join Denmark in entering the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (later absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>). The islands experienced considerable economic difficulties following the collapse of the fishing industry in the early 1990s, but have since made efforts to <a href="/wiki/Diversity_(business)" title="Diversity (business)">diversify</a> the economy. Support for independence has grown and is the objective of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_(Faroe_Islands)" title="Republic (Faroe Islands)">Republican Party</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Geography of the Faroe Islands">Geography of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faroes030417-nasa(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="605" data-file-width="409" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Faroes030417-nasa%282%29.jpg/170px-Faroes030417-nasa%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Faroes030417-nasa%282%29.jpg/255px-Faroes030417-nasa%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Faroes030417-nasa%282%29.jpg/340px-Faroes030417-nasa%282%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faroes030417-nasa(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
NASA satellite image of the Faroe Islands</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Faroe Islands are an island group consisting of 18 major islands about 655 kilometres (407 mi) off the coast of Northern Europe, between the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Sea" title="Norwegian Sea">Norwegian Sea</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="North Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a>, about halfway between <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, the closest neighbours being the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Isles" title="Northern Isles">Northern Isles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a> of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. Its coordinates are <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Faroe_Islands&amp;params=62_00_N_06_47_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">62°00′N</span> <span class="longitude">06°47′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">62.000°N 6.783°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">62.000; -6.783</span></span></span></a></span>.</p>
<p>Distance from the Faroe Islands to:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_Rona" title="North Rona">North Rona</a>, Scotland (uninhabited): 260 kilometres (160 mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> (<a href="/wiki/Foula" title="Foula">Foula</a>), Scotland: 285 kilometres (177 mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> (<a href="/wiki/Westray" title="Westray">Westray</a>), Scotland: 300 kilometres (190 mi)</li>
<li>Scotland (mainland): 320 kilometres (200 mi)</li>
<li>Iceland: 450 kilometres (280 mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>: 670 kilometres (420 mi)</li>
<li>Norway: 670 kilometres (420 mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>: 990 kilometres (620 mi)</li>
</ul>
<p>The islands cover an area of 1,399 square kilometres (540 sq. mi) and have <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="List of lakes of the Faroe Islands">small lakes</a> and rivers, but no major ones. There are 1,117 kilometres (694 mi) of coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook-19">[19]</a></sup> The only significant uninhabited island is <a href="/wiki/L%C3%ADtla_D%C3%ADmun" title="Lítla Dímun">Lítla Dímun</a>.</p>
<p>The islands are rugged and rocky with some low peaks; the coasts are mostly cliffs. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Sl%C3%A6ttaratindur" title="Slættaratindur">Slættaratindur</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Eysturoy" title="Eysturoy">Eysturoy</a>, 882 metres (2,894 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>.</p>
<p>The Faroe Islands are dominated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tholeiitic_basalt" title="Tholeiitic basalt">tholeiitic basalt</a> <a href="/wiki/Lava" title="Lava">lava</a>, which was part of the great <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Igneous_Province" title="North Atlantic Igneous Province">Thulean Plateau</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Paleogene" title="Paleogene">Paleogene</a> period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_Islands,_Eysturoy,_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1282" data-file-width="1930" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg/220px-Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg/330px-Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg/440px-Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_Islands,_Eysturoy,_Skipanes_and_Undir_G%C3%B8tuei%C3%B0i.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Skipanes" title="Skipanes">Skipanes</a> on <a href="/wiki/Eysturoy" title="Eysturoy">Eysturoy</a>, with different weather in the distance</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate is classed as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subpolar_oceanic_climate" title="Subpolar oceanic climate">subpolar oceanic climate</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Cfc</a>, with areas having a <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> climate, especially in the mountains, although some coastal or low-lying areas can have very mild-winter versions of a tundra climate. The overall character of the islands' climate is influenced by the strong warming influence of the Atlantic Ocean, which produces the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Current" title="North Atlantic Current">North Atlantic Current</a>. This, together with the remoteness of any source of warm airflows, ensures that winters are mild (mean temperature 3.0 to 4.0 °C or 37 to 39 °F) while summers are cool (mean temperature 9.5 to 10.5 °C or 49 to 51 °F).</p>
<p>The islands are windy, cloudy and cool throughout the year with an average of 210 rainy or snowy days per year. The islands lie in the path of depressions moving northeast, making strong winds and heavy rain possible at all times of the year. Sunny days are rare and overcast days are common. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Faith" title="Hurricane Faith">Hurricane Faith</a> struck the Faroe Islands on 5 September 1966 with sustained winds over 100 mph (160 km/h) and only then did the storm cease to be a tropical system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_Islands,_Eysturoy,_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_(fjord)_in_October.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="928" data-file-width="2144" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_%28fjord%29_in_October.jpg/220px-Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_%28fjord%29_in_October.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_%28fjord%29_in_October.jpg/330px-Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_%28fjord%29_in_October.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_%28fjord%29_in_October.jpg/440px-Faroe_Islands%2C_Eysturoy%2C_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_%28fjord%29_in_October.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_Islands,_Eysturoy,_Funningsfj%C3%B8r%C3%B0ur_(fjord)_in_October.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An October evening on <a href="/wiki/Eysturoy" title="Eysturoy">Eysturoy</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate varies greatly over small distances, due to the altitude, ocean currents, topography and winds. Precipitation varies considerably throughout the archipelago. In some highland areas, snow cover can last for months with snowfalls possible for the greater part of the year (on the highest peaks, summer snowfall is by no means rare), while in some sheltered coastal locations, several years pass without any snowfall whatsoever. Tórshavn receives frosts more often than other areas just a short distance to the south. Snow is also seen at a much higher frequency than on outlying islands nearby. The area receives on average 49 frosts a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMI-1_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-DMI-1-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The collection of meteorological data on the Faroe Islands began in 1867.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Winter recording began in 1891, and the warmest winter occurred in 2016-17 with an average temperature of 6.1 °C.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature">Nature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A collection of Faroese marine <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a> resulting from a survey sponsored by <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a> (Natural History) and the Carlsberg Foundation, is preserved in the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Museum" title="Ulster Museum">Ulster Museum</a> (catalogue numbers: F3195–F3307). It is one of ten exsiccatae sets.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Flora of the Faroe Islands">Flora of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Myrisolja.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Myrisolja.jpg/220px-Myrisolja.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Myrisolja.jpg/330px-Myrisolja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Myrisolja.jpg/440px-Myrisolja.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Myrisolja.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Marsh marigold (<i><a href="/wiki/Caltha_palustris" title="Caltha palustris">Caltha palustris</a></i>) is common in the Faroe Islands during May and June.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The natural vegetation of the Faroe Islands is dominated by arctic-alpine plants, wildflowers, grasses, moss and lichen. Most of the lowland area is grassland and some is heath, dominated by shrubby heathers, mainly <a href="/wiki/Calluna" title="Calluna"><i>Calluna vulgaris</i></a>. Among the herbaceous flora that occur in the Faroe Islands is the cosmopolitan marsh thistle, <i><a href="/wiki/Cirsium_palustre" title="Cirsium palustre">Cirsium palustre</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although there are no trees native to the Faroe Islands, limited species were able to be successfully introduced to the region, including the <a href="/wiki/Populus_trichocarpa#Distribution" title="Populus trichocarpa">Black Cottonwood</a>, also known as the <a href="/wiki/Populus_trichocarpa#Distribution" title="Populus trichocarpa">California Poplar (Populus trichocarpa)</a></p>
<p>A few small plantations consisting of plants collected from similar climates such as <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a> in South America and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> thrive on the islands.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Fauna of the Faroe Islands">Fauna of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dreierprofil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Dreierprofil.jpg/220px-Dreierprofil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Dreierprofil.jpg/330px-Dreierprofil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Dreierprofil.jpg/440px-Dreierprofil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dreierprofil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Faroese_puffin" title="Faroese puffin">Faroese puffins</a> are very common and a part of the local cuisine.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="List of birds of the Faroe Islands">List of birds of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="List of birds of the Faroe Islands">bird fauna of the Faroe Islands</a> is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Seabird" title="Seabird">seabirds</a> and birds attracted to open land like <a href="/wiki/Calluna" title="Calluna">heather</a>, probably because of the lack of woodland and other suitable habitats. Many species have developed special Faroese sub-species: <a href="/wiki/Common_eider" title="Common eider">common eider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_starling" title="Common starling">Common starling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_wren" title="Eurasian wren">Eurasian wren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_murre" title="Common murre">common murre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Black_guillemot" title="Black guillemot">black guillemot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pied_raven" title="Pied raven">pied raven</a> was <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to the Faroe Islands, but has now become extinct.</p>
<p>Only a few species of wild land mammals are found in the Faroe Islands today, all introduced by humans. Three species are thriving on the islands today: <a href="/wiki/Mountain_hare" title="Mountain hare">mountain hare</a> (<i>Lepus timidus</i>), <a href="/wiki/Brown_rat" title="Brown rat">brown rat</a> (<i>Rattus norvegicus</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/House_mouse" title="House mouse">house mouse</a> (<i>Mus musculus</i>). Apart from these, there once was a local domestic sheep breed, the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_sheep" title="Faroe sheep">Faroe sheep</a> (depicted on the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Coat of arms of the Faroe Islands">coat of arms</a>), a variety of <a href="/wiki/Feral_animal" title="Feral animal">feral sheep</a> survived on <a href="/wiki/L%C3%ADtla_D%C3%ADmun" title="Lítla Dímun">Lítla Dímun</a> until the mid-19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hvalba_scenery.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2560" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Hvalba_scenery.jpg/220px-Hvalba_scenery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Hvalba_scenery.jpg/330px-Hvalba_scenery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Hvalba_scenery.jpg/440px-Hvalba_scenery.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hvalba_scenery.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Faroese sheep</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">Grey seals</a> (<i>Halichoerus grypus</i>) are common around the shorelines.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Several species of <a href="/wiki/Cetacea" title="Cetacea">cetacea</a> live in the waters around the Faroe Islands. Best known are the <a href="/wiki/Long-finned_pilot_whale" title="Long-finned pilot whale">long-finned pilot whales</a> (<i>Globicephala melaena</i>), which are still hunted by the islanders in accordance with longstanding local tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Killer_whale" title="Killer whale">Killer whales</a> (<i>Orcinus orca</i>) are regular visitors around the islands.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands_domestic_animals" title="Faroe Islands domestic animals">domestic animals of the Faroe Islands</a> are a result of 1,200 years of isolated breeding. As a result, many of the islands' domestic animals are found nowhere else in the world. Faroese domestic breed include <a href="/wiki/Faroe_pony" title="Faroe pony">Faroe pony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands_domestic_animals#Faroese_cow" title="Faroe Islands domestic animals">Faroe cow</a>, Faroe sheep, <a href="/wiki/Faroese_goose" title="Faroese goose">Faroese goose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands_domestic_animals#Faroese_duck" title="Faroe Islands domestic animals">Faroese duck</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Politics of the Faroe Islands">Politics of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Faroese_general_election,_2015" title="Faroese general election, 2015">Faroese general election, 2015</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tinganes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tinganes.jpg/220px-Tinganes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tinganes.jpg/330px-Tinganes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tinganes.jpg/440px-Tinganes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tinganes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tinganes" title="Tinganes">Tinganes</a> in <a href="/wiki/T%C3%B3rshavn" title="Tórshavn">Tórshavn</a>, seat of a part of the Faroese government</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Faroese government holds <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">executive power</a> in local government affairs. The head of the government is called the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%B8gma%C3%B0ur" title="Løgmaður">Løgmaður</a></i> ("Law person") and serves as a premier. Any other member of the cabinet is called a <i><a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">landsstýrismaður</a></i> ("national committee man") or <i>landsstýriskvinna</i> ("national committee woman"). The Faroese parliament – the <i><a href="/wiki/L%C3%B8gting" title="Løgting">Løgting</a></i> ("Law assembly") – dates back to Viking times and is believed to be one of the oldest parliaments in the world. The parliament currently has 33 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In contemporary times, elections are held at municipal, national (<i><a href="/wiki/L%C3%B8gting" title="Løgting">Løgting</a></i>) and Danish (<i><a href="/wiki/Folketing" title="Folketing">Folketing</a></i>) levels. Until 2007, there were seven electoral districts, each comprising a <i>sýsla</i>, while Streymoy was divided into a northern and southern part (<a href="/wiki/T%C3%B3rshavn" title="Tórshavn">Tórshavn</a> region). However, on 25 October 2007, changes were made such that the entire country is one electoral district, giving each vote equal weight.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Regions of the Faroe Islands">Regions of the Faroe Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Municipalities of the Faroe Islands">Municipalities of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2208" data-file-width="1683" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg/220px-Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg/330px-Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg/440px-Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Faroe_Islands_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Relief map of the Faroe Islands</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Administratively, the islands are divided into 30 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Municipalities of the Faroe Islands">municipalities</a> (<i>kommunur</i>) within which there are 120 or so <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_in_the_Faroe_Islands" title="List of towns in the Faroe Islands">settlements</a>.</p>
<p>Traditionally, there are also the <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Regions of the Faroe Islands">six <i>sýslur</i></a> (similar to the British "shire": <a href="/wiki/Nor%C3%B0oyar" title="Norðoyar">Norðoyar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eysturoy" title="Eysturoy">Eysturoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Streymoy" title="Streymoy">Streymoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1gar" title="Vágar">Vágar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandoy" title="Sandoy">Sandoy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Su%C3%B0uroy" title="Suðuroy">Suðuroy</a>). Although today <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BDsla" title="Sýsla">sýsla</a></i> technically means "police district", the term is still commonly used to indicate a geographical region. In earlier times, each <i>sýsla</i> had its own <a href="/wiki/Thing_(assembly)" title="Thing (assembly)">assembly</a>, the so-called <i>várting</i> ("spring assembly").</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_Denmark">Relationship with Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Relationship with Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Faroe Islands have been under Norwegian/Danish control since 1388. The 1814 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kiel" title="Treaty of Kiel">Treaty of Kiel</a> terminated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denmark-Norway" title="Denmark-Norway">Danish-Norwegian</a> union, and Norway came under the rule of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Sweden" title="King of Sweden">King of Sweden</a>, while the Faroe Islands, Iceland and <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> remained Danish possessions. From ancient times the Faroe Islands had a parliament (<i>Løgting</i>) which was abolished in 1816, and the Faroe Islands were to be governed as an ordinary <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Denmark" title="Counties of Denmark">Danish amt</a> (county), with the <a href="/wiki/Prefect" title="Prefect">Amtmand</a> as its head of government. In 1851, the <i>Løgting</i> was reinstated, but, until 1948, served mainly as an advisory body.</p>
<p>The islands are home to a notable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faroese_independence" title="Faroese independence">independence movement</a> that has seen an increase in popularity within recent decades. At the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, some of the population favoured independence from Denmark, and on 14 September 1946 <a href="/wiki/Faroese_independence_referendum,_1946" title="Faroese independence referendum, 1946">an independence referendum</a> was held on the question of <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a>. It was a consultative referendum; the parliament was not bound to follow the people's vote. This was the first time that the Faroese people had been asked whether they favoured independence or wanted to continue within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_kingdom" title="Danish kingdom">Danish kingdom</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg/220px-Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg/330px-Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg/440px-Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Margrethe_21-06-2005_V%C3%A1gur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II</a>, monarch of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unity_of_the_Realm" title="Unity of the Realm">Unity of the Realm</a>, during a visit to <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1gur" title="Vágur">Vágur</a> in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The result of the vote was a narrow majority in favour of secession, but the coalition in parliament could not reach agreement on how this outcome should be interpreted and implemented; and because of these irresoluble differences, the <a href="/wiki/Coalition" title="Coalition">coalition</a> fell apart. A parliamentary election was held a few months later, in which the political parties that favoured staying in the Danish kingdom increased their share of the vote and formed a coalition. Based on this, they chose to reject secession. Instead, a compromise was made and the <a href="/wiki/Folketing" title="Folketing">Folketing</a> passed a home-rule law that went into effect in 1948. The Faroe Islands' status as a Danish <i>amt</i> was thereby brought to an end; the Faroe Islands were given a high degree of self-governance, supported by a financial <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">subsidy</a> from Denmark to recompense expenses the islands have on Danish services.</p>
<p>At present, the islanders are about evenly split between those favouring independence and those who prefer to continue as a part of the Kingdom of Denmark. Within both camps there is a wide range of opinions. Of those who favour independence, some are in favour of an immediate <a href="/wiki/Unilateral_declaration_of_independence" title="Unilateral declaration of independence">unilateral declaration of independence</a>. Others see it as something to be attained gradually and with the full consent of the Danish government and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_nation" title="Danish nation">Danish nation</a>. In the unionist camp there are also many who foresee and welcome a gradual increase in autonomy even while strong ties with Denmark are maintained.</p>
<p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a new draft Faroese constitution is being drawn up. However the draft has been declared by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_Prime_Minister" title="Danish Prime Minister">Danish Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen" title="Lars Løkke Rasmussen">Lars Løkke Rasmussen</a>, as incompatible with Denmark's constitution and if the Faroese political parties wish to continue with it then they must declare independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_the_European_Union">Relationship with the European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Relationship with the European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands_and_the_European_Union" title="Faroe Islands and the European Union">Faroe Islands and the European Union</a></div>
<p>As explicitly asserted by both <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties of the European Union</a>, the Faroe Islands are not part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The Faroes are not grouped with the EU when it comes to international trade; for instance, when the EU and Russia imposed reciprocal trade sanctions on each other over the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">War in Donbass</a> in 2014, the Faroes began exporting significant amounts of fresh <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> to Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Moreover, a <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union#Faroe_Islands" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">protocol</a> to the treaty of accession of Denmark to the European Communities stipulates that Danish nationals residing in the Faroe Islands are not considered Danish nationals within the meaning of the treaties. Hence, Danish people living in the Faroes are not <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">citizens of the European Union</a> (though other EU nationals living there remain EU citizens). The Faroes are not covered by the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a>, but there are no border checks when travelling between the Faroes and any Schengen country (the Faroes have been part of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Passport_Union" title="Nordic Passport Union">Nordic Passport Union</a> since 1966, and since 2001 there have been no permanent border checks between the Nordic countries and the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> as part of the Schengen agreement).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_international_organisations">Relationship with international organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Relationship with international organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Faroe Islands are not a fully independent country, but they do have political relations directly with other countries through agreement with Denmark. The Faroe Islands are a member of some international organisations as though they were an independent country.</p>
<p>The Faroe Islands are a member of several international sports federations like <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>, <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> in <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/FINA" title="FINA">FINA</a> in swimming<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and EHF in <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and have their own national teams. The Faroe Islands have their own telephone country code, Internet country code top-level domain, banking code and postal country code.</p>
<p>The Faroe Islands make their own agreements with other countries regarding trade and commerce. When the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> embargo against <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> started in 2014, the Faroe Islands were not a part of the embargo because they are not a part of EU, and the islands had just themselves experienced a year of embargo from the EU including Denmark against the islands; the Faroese prime minister <a href="/wiki/Kaj_Leo_Johannesen" title="Kaj Leo Johannesen">Kaj Leo Johannesen</a> went to <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> to negotiate the trade between the two countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Embargo2014_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Embargo2014-8">[8]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ministers_of_Fisheries_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="List of Ministers of Fisheries of the Faroe Islands">Faroese minister of fisheries</a> negotiates with the EU and other countries regarding the rights to fish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Demographics of the Faroe Islands">Demographics of the Faroe Islands</a></div>

<p>The vast majority of the population are <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islanders" title="Faroe Islanders">ethnic Faroese</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celts_(modern)" title="Celts (modern)">Celtic</a> descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Recent DNA analyses have revealed that Y chromosomes, tracing male descent, are 87% <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The studies show that <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA" title="Mitochondrial DNA">mitochondrial DNA</a>, tracing female descent, is 84% <a href="/wiki/Celts_(modern)" title="Celts (modern)">Celtic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a gender deficit of about 2,000 women owing to migration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-43">[43]</a></sup> Three hundred women from the Philippines and Thailand, recruited as wives because of the Faroes' gender imbalance, make up the largest ethnic minority in the Faroes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of the Faroe Islands is currently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_fertility_rate" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by fertility rate">one of the highest</a> in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The fertility rate is 2.409 children born per woman (2015 est.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Faroe_Islands_in_Figures_2016_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Faroe_Islands_in_Figures_2016-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2011 census shows that of the approximately 48,600 inhabitants of the Faroe Islands (17,441 private households in 2011), 43,135 were born in the Faroe Islands, 3,597 were born in the other two countries of the Kingdom of Denmark (Denmark or Greenland), and 1,614 were born outside the Kingdom of Denmark. People were also asked about their nationality, including Faroese. Children under 15 were not asked about their nationality. 97% said that they were ethnic Faroese, which means that many of those who were born in either Denmark or Greenland consider themselves as ethnic Faroese. The other 3% of those older than 15 said they were not Faroese: 515 were Danish, 433 were from other European countries, 147 came from Asia, 65 from Africa, 55 from the Americas, 23 from Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_census.2C_born_in_other_countries_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011_census.2C_born_in_other_countries-46">[46]</a></sup> The Faroe Islands have people from 77 different nationalities.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_stamp_360_arrival_of_christianity.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="244" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Faroe_stamp_360_arrival_of_christianity.jpg/170px-Faroe_stamp_360_arrival_of_christianity.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Faroe_stamp_360_arrival_of_christianity.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_stamp_360_arrival_of_christianity.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Faroese stamp by <a href="/wiki/Anker_Eli_Petersen" title="Anker Eli Petersen">Anker Eli Petersen</a> commemorating the arrival of Christianity in the islands</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>If the first inhabitants of the Faroe Islands were <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> monks, then they must have lived as a very small group of settlers. Later, when the Vikings colonised the islands, there was a considerable increase in the population. However, it never exceeded 5,000 until the 19th century. Around 1349, about half the population perished in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> plague.</p>
<p>Only with the rise of the deep-sea fishery (and thus independence from agriculture in the islands' harsh terrain) and with general progress in the health service was rapid population growth possible in the Faroes. Beginning in the 19th century, the population increased tenfold in 200 years.</p>
<p>At the beginning of the 1990s, the Faroe Islands entered a deep economic crisis leading to heavy emigration; however, this trend reversed in subsequent years to a net immigration. This has been in the form of a population replacement as young Faroese women leave and are replaced with Asian/Pacific brides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In 2011 there were 2,155 more men than women between the age of 0 to 59 in the Faroe Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Faroese population is spread across most of the area; it was not until recent decades that significant urbanisation occurred. Industrialisation has been remarkably decentralised, and the area has therefore maintained quite a viable rural culture. Nevertheless, villages with poor harbour facilities have been the losers in the development from agriculture to fishing, and in the most peripheral agricultural areas, also known as <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Atoyggjar" title="Útoyggjar">Útoyggjar</a> "Outer Islands", there are few young people. In recent decades, the village-based social structure has nevertheless been placed under pressure, giving way to a rise in interconnected "centres" that are better able to provide goods and services than the badly connected periphery. This means that shops and services are now relocating en masse from the villages into the centres, and slowly but steadily the Faroese population is concentrating in and around the centres.</p>
<p>In the 1990s, the government abandoned the old national policy of developing the villages (Bygdamenning), and instead began a process of regional development (Økismenning). The term "region" referred to the large islands of the Faroes. Nevertheless, the government was unable to press through the structural reform of merging small rural municipalities to create sustainable, decentralised entities that could drive forward regional development. As regional development has been difficult on the administrative level, the government has instead invested heavily in infrastructure, interconnecting the regions.</p>
<p>In general, it is becoming less valid to regard the Faroes as a society based on separate islands and regions. The huge investments in roads, bridges and sub-sea tunnels (see also <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Transport in the Faroe Islands">Transport in the Faroe Islands</a>) have bound the islands together, creating a coherent economic and cultural sphere that covers almost 90% of the population. From this perspective it is reasonable to regard the Faroes as a dispersed city or even to refer to it as the <i>Faroese Network City</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_stamp_048_europe_(v_u_hammershaimb).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="265" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Faroe_stamp_048_europe_%28v_u_hammershaimb%29.jpg/170px-Faroe_stamp_048_europe_%28v_u_hammershaimb%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Faroe_stamp_048_europe_%28v_u_hammershaimb%29.jpg/255px-Faroe_stamp_048_europe_%28v_u_hammershaimb%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Faroe_stamp_048_europe_%28v_u_hammershaimb%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faroe_stamp_048_europe_(v_u_hammershaimb).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A stamp commemorating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V._U._Hammershaimb" title="V. U. Hammershaimb">V. U. Hammershaimb</a>, a 19th-century Faroese linguist and theologian</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Languages of the Faroe Islands">Languages of the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a> is spoken in the entire area as a first language. It is difficult to say exactly how many people worldwide speak the Faroese language, because many ethnic Faroese live in Denmark, and few who are born there return to the Faroes with their parents or as adults.</p>
<p>The Faroese language is one of the smallest of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a>. Written Faroese (grammar and vocabulary) is most similar to <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> and to their ancestor <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a>, though the spoken language is closer to <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> dialects of <a href="/wiki/Western_Norway" title="Western Norway">Western Norway</a>. Although Faroese is the official language on the islands, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a> is taught in schools and can be used by the Faroese government in public relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-folang_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-folang-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Faroese language policy provides for the active creation of new terms in Faroese suitable for modern life.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Religion in the Faroe Islands">Religion in the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A6reyinga_saga" title="Færeyinga saga">Færeyinga saga</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Sigmundur_Brestisson" title="Sigmundur Brestisson">Sigmundur Brestisson</a> brought Christianity to the islands in 999. However, archaeology at a site in Toftanes, <a href="/wiki/Leirv%C3%ADk" title="Leirvík">Leirvík</a> named Bønhústoftin (English: prayer-house ruin) and over a dozen slabs from Ólansgarður in the small island of <a href="/wiki/Sk%C3%BAvoy" title="Skúvoy">Skúvoy</a> which in the main display encircled linear and outline crosses, suggest that <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Christianity" title="Celtic Christianity">Celtic Christianity</a> may have arrived at least 150 years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B.C3.B8nh.C3.BAstoftin_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-B.C3.B8nh.C3.BAstoftin-49">[49]</a></sup> The Faroe Islands' Church <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> was completed on 1 January 1540. According to official statistics from 2002, 84.1% of the Faroese population are members of the state church, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Church of the Faroe Islands">Church of the Faroe Islands</a> (Fólkakirkjan), a form of <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a>. The Fólkakirkjan became an independent church in 2007; previously it had been a diocese within the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">Church of Denmark</a>. Faroese members of the clergy who have had historical importance include <a href="/wiki/Venceslaus_Ulricus_Hammershaimb" title="Venceslaus Ulricus Hammershaimb">Venceslaus Ulricus Hammershaimb</a> (1819–1909), <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%AD%C3%B0rikur_Petersen" title="Fríðrikur Petersen">Fríðrikur Petersen</a> (1853–1917) and, perhaps most significantly, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1kup_Dahl" title="Jákup Dahl">Jákup Dahl</a> (1878–1944), who had a great influence in ensuring that the <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese language</a> was spoken in the church instead of <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>. Participation in churches is more prevalent among the Faroese population than among most other Scandinavians.</p>
<p>In the late 1820s, the Christian <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> religious movement, the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">Plymouth Brethren</a>, was established in England. In 1865, a member of this movement, <a href="/wiki/William_Gibson_Sloan" title="William Gibson Sloan">William Gibson Sloan</a>, travelled to the Faroes from <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>. At the turn of the 20th century, the Faroese Plymouth Brethren numbered thirty. Today, around 10% of the Faroese population are members of the Open Brethren community (<i>Brøðrasamkoman</i>). About 3% belong to the <a href="/wiki/Charismatic_Movement" title="Charismatic Movement">Charismatic Movement</a>. There are several charismatic churches around the islands, the largest of which, called Keldan (The Spring), has about 200 to 300 members. About 2% belong to other Christian groups. The <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">Adventists</a> operate a private school in Tórshavn. <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> also have four congregations with a total of 121 members. The Roman Catholic congregation has about 170 members and falls under the jurisdiction of Denmark's <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Copenhagen" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Copenhagen">Roman Catholic Diocese of Copenhagen</a>. The municipality of <a href="/wiki/T%C3%B3rshavn" title="Tórshavn">Tórshavn</a> has an old <a href="/wiki/Franciscans" title="Franciscans">Franciscan</a> school.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kunoy,_Faroe_Islands_(2).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2560" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Kunoy%2C_Faroe_Islands_%282%29.JPG/220px-Kunoy%2C_Faroe_Islands_%282%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Kunoy%2C_Faroe_Islands_%282%29.JPG/330px-Kunoy%2C_Faroe_Islands_%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Kunoy%2C_Faroe_Islands_%282%29.JPG/440px-Kunoy%2C_Faroe_Islands_%282%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kunoy,_Faroe_Islands_(2).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Church in <a href="/wiki/Kunoy" title="Kunoy">Kunoy</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are also around fifteen <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'ís</a> who meet at four different places. The <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyyas</a> established a community in the Faroe Islands in 2010. Unlike <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> with <a href="/wiki/Heathenry_(new_religious_movement)#Forn_Si.C3.B0r" title="Heathenry (new religious movement)">Forn Siðr</a>, the Faroes have no organised Heathen community.</p>
<p>The best-known church buildings in the Faroe Islands include <a href="/wiki/T%C3%B3rshavn_Cathedral" title="Tórshavn Cathedral">Tórshavn Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olaf_II_of_Norway" title="Olaf II of Norway">Olaf II of Norway</a>'s Church and the <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Cathedral" title="Magnus Cathedral">Magnus Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kirkjub%C3%B8ur" title="Kirkjubøur">Kirkjubøur</a>; the Vesturkirkjan and the Maria Church, both of which are situated in Tórshavn; the church of <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A1mjin" title="Fámjin">Fámjin</a>; the octagonal church in <a href="/wiki/Hald%C3%B3rsv%C3%ADk" title="Haldórsvík">Haldórsvík</a>; Christianskirkjan in <a href="/wiki/Klaksv%C3%ADk" title="Klaksvík">Klaksvík</a>; and also the two pictured here.</p>
<p>In 1948, Victor Danielsen (Plymouth Brethren) completed the first Bible translation into Faroese from different modern languages. Jacob Dahl and Kristian Osvald Viderø (Fólkakirkjan) completed the second translation in 1961. The latter was translated from the original Biblical languages (<a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>) into Faroese.</p>
<p>According to the 2011 Census, there were 33,018 Christians (95.44%), 23 Muslims (0.07%), 7 <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> (0.02%), 66 <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a> (0.19%), 12 <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (0.03%), 13 Baha'i (0.04%), 3 <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhs</a> (0.01%), 149 others (0.43%), 85 with more than one belief (0.25%) and 1397 with no religion (4.04%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Faroe_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Education in the Faroe Islands">Education in the Faroe Islands</a></div>
<p>The levels of education in the Faroe Islands are <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher</a> education. Most institutions are funded by the state; there are few private schools in the country. Education is compulsory for 9 years between the ages of 7 and 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-educationfaroe_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-educationfaroe-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Compulsory education consists of seven years of primary education and two years of lower secondary education; it is public, free of charge, provided by the respective municipalities, and is called the Fólkaskúli in Faroese. The Fólkaskúli also provides optional preschool education as well as the tenth year of education that is a prerequisite to get admitted to upper secondary education. Students that complete compulsory education are allowed to continue education in a <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">vocational school</a>, where they can have job-specific training and education. Since the fishing industry is an important part of <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Economy of the Faroe Islands">country's economy</a>, maritime schools are an important part of Faroese education. Upon completion of the tenth year of Fólkaskúli, students can continue to upper secondary education which consists of several different types of schools. Higher education is offered at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="University of the Faroe Islands">University of the Faroe Islands</a>; a part of Faroese youth moves abroad to pursue higher education, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>. Other forms of education comprise <a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">adult education</a> and music schools. The structure of the Faroese educational system bears resemblances with its Danish counterpart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-educationfaroe_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-educationfaroe-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/12th_century" title="12th century">12th century</a>, education was provided by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Catholic Church in the Faroe Islands">Catholic Church in the Faroe Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Debes_2000_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Debes_2000-52">[52]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">Church of Denmark</a> took over education after the <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Denmark%E2%80%93Norway_and_Holstein" title="Reformation in Denmark–Norway and Holstein">Protestant Reformation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Debes_2000.2C_chapter_2_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Debes_2000.2C_chapter_2-53">[53]</a></sup> Modern educational institutions started operating in the last quarter of the nineteenth century and developed throughout the twentieth century. The status of the Faroese language in education was a significant issue for decades, until it was accepted as a language of instruction in 1938.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cultral_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-cultral-54">[54]</a></sup> Initially education was administered and regulated by Denmark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cultral_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-cultral-54">[54]</a></sup> In 1979 responsibilities on educational issues started transferring to the Faroese authorities, a procedure which was completed in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cultral_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-cultral-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Research_and_Culture_(Faroe_Islands)" title="Ministry of Education, Research and Culture (Faroe Islands)">Ministry of Education, Research and Culture</a> has the jurisdiction of educational responsibility in the Faroe Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government-education_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-government-education-55">[55]</a></sup> Since the Faroe Islands is a constituent country of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" title="Danish Realm">Danish Realm</a>, education in the Faroe Islands is influenced and has similarities with the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Denmark" title="Education in Denmark">Danish educational system</a>;
